**作者** 冰河（@binghe）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/binghe/status/2016434536142586157  

**正文**

今天的教程非常有实战意义，这并不等同于那些工具型，提升效率型的 Skills，而是直接可以拿来就用，用了就可以创收的实用型 Skill！

AI 写小说这个课题在以前，我们写过很多相关文章，AI 网文写作指令都已经升级到了 3.0，每次的迭代都是我们对小说写作的一次认知梳理！（文章在“钱来有道”公众号查看）

废话不多说，开始今天的教程！

上次已经发布了：

没看过的，可以先看一下，社群内部已经发布了这个 Skill。

今天讲的是如何使用 Skill 写长篇小说!

AI写长篇小说有几个常见问题，我想如果你们使用过我以前的指令就会感觉出来：

1，随着写作的内容越来越多，AI产生幻觉的可能性就越大。

2，如果使用 Claude 网页端，“项目”写作的话，当你的篇章和设定非常多的时候，项目内的文档存储上限就会爆表！需要不断的删减，这样又会导致 AI对以前剧情和角色关系的混乱。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_ulPzsbAAIiLNr.jpg>)

3，单纯的让 AI 写作，出大纲会让网文小说非常的格式化，AI 味重，水词也会相应增加，导致很多人上传小说后，被平台审核，严重的话直接封号。

4，从没有写过网文的小白，只知道用 AI 配合指令无脑写网文，却忽视了扫榜了解当年最流行的主题和爽点设计风格，这也是 AI 写作的弊端！

5，小说的大纲，细纲，角色档案和角色关系，是一部小说的根基，前期混乱或不常更新就会导致后期写作跑偏！

针对以上五点，最为常见也最重要的痛点，下面的这个 Skill 会针对性的一一解决！

## 这个长篇小说 Skill 有以下几个特点：

1，写作初期，与用户一同确认主题风格，如果你未扫过榜了解市场需求，AI 可以配合你给出扫榜注意事项，或者让它根据 Skill 里的规则，直接扫榜，产出扫榜结果的文档留存，便于以后你自己学习或引用查看。

2，在产出角色档案（小传），角色关系，大纲后，都会生成文档，放入写作项目文件夹中，便于以后调取。

并且大纲生成后会问询是否需要细纲的设定，有大纲，只是方向，而细刚就是你对 AI 产出内容的一个大体判断，通过不断的优化细纲，这样产出的小说文章会更有针对性。

3，网文小说，每章大概 3000 字左右，长篇小说一般是 50--150 万字左右，知名小说就上不封顶了。

但如果要保持 50 万字的小说写作不走样，就需要 Skill 每次写作前对以前产出内容，都做一下回顾，这样输出的小说就不会产生幻觉，也会轻松续写。

4，增加了去 AI 味，去水词的规则设定，你只要通过几个指令，就可以对产出内容进行审核，即使如此，我个人还是建议，去掉 AI 味后，你自己也要参与进来，再二次润色，这样的文章才真正的赋予了人味。

好，我们开始实战流程：

第一步，新建一个项目文件夹xiaoshuo（用于存放小说设定和文章内容）

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_uqqRpbEAEb5Hm.jpg>)

第二步，把 Skill 文件，放到全局 Skills 里，也可以放在你新建的项目文件夹里！都可以

区别就是：放全局是以后经常写直接调用，放项目文件夹里，是只为本小说单独调用！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_upPJ3asAAVo93.jpg>)

如果找不到全局文件夹，我以苹果电脑为例：

> 在访达菜里里，找到 -- 前往 -- 前往文件夹 -- 输入“~/.claude”

进去后，找到上图中的 Skills 里，把这个 Skill 文件夹直接拖放进去就可以了。

第三步，在新建的 xiaoshuo 文件夹里打开 claude 命令窗口！

看我上面的教程中，有个Claude Code Now，它是一个 Claude 启动器，@oran\_ge 桔子开发的，非常好用（上图小红框处），点击那个 Claude 的小图标，就可以直接在这个文件夹里打开了。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_urs__XQAAgTb2.jpg>)

可以看到，首先，我们是在 xiaoshuo 的文件夹中启动的 claude code

直接输入：我要写长篇小说，相到相关 skill 在本文件夹中开始小说的创作。

然后他就找到了我们放在全局里的技能包：novel-writing-skill 开始了创作流程。

就这么简单！

接下来，输入“开始”启动写作流程！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_usgPdXwAAXpRY.jpg>)

创作想法和题材方向，你根据自己的情况，上下选择，或者在第 4 条直接输入你的想法。

选择好后回车。

我这里为了让你体验市场调研的流程，所以选择的是第 1 个，后期你有经验了，可以自由选择！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_utgn_aEAAbwbq.jpg>)

我强烈推荐你走一下 AI 协助扫榜流程，然后你就会知道扫榜到底是什么意思，为什么新手写作前一定要扫榜的重要性。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_uwcCebAAI9euf.jpg>)

生成结果，直接放入项目文件夹中，你可以打开看看详细报告。

然后根据网调给出下面的近期热门题材，你可以选择，也可以按自己的想法来，完全自由！

我个人建议还是跟着潮流走吧，很多小白写文没人看，就是孤芳自赏！

我选择了最热门的第一个选项，继续下面的流程，文笔风格选择！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_uxFzcbwAAq4Me.jpg>)

这里不做重点说明，自己定就行，如果想参考其它作者的文风，就选择 5 告诉 AI你希望是那部作品的笔风，他会自行找到判断！个人不太建议！

容易被判定为抄袭！

接下来，它会把上面的题材选择和写作风格进行确定，并生成文档，以供日后写作参考，在 xiaoshuo 文件夹中生成style-guide.md 文档！

后面就下一步，确定主角信息之类的内容，我就不截图了，你们每人选择的题材不一样，看到的结果也不一样。

但要说明一下，如果觉的这里给的选择比较细，你不想这么麻烦，也可以跳过，直接让他进行下一步！

在主角这里的设计，你可以用点心和他共创，比如：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_uzDfEbEAAcuOB.jpg>)

因为这里有个金手指设计，网文小说的金手指就是一部作品的灵魂，所有的反转，爽点都是围绕它来展开的！

一路选择，回车，再到最后的提交，就是这么简单丝滑！剩下的让它自己去费 token 去，会自动生成小说设定的文档，我们就去喝杯茶，坐等下一步！

如果中间没意外的话，我们就到了大纲设计环节！

其实大家不要太在意这个大纲，先出大纲是让你对整个小说的故事线更清晰，后期还是要不断修改大纲的，所以，让它直出就行！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_vKZXkbAAEbxxk.jpg>)

可以看到，已经生成的文档都已经放到了项目文件夹里。

大纲你可以去打开细看一下，如果有问题，随时中断，让他修改都行。

接下来是“角色档案”生成，这里包括的是：主角、配角、反派等，还有他们之间的人物关系！非常重要，角色档案也叫人物小传！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_u3RuBbAAI0h_E.jpg>)

你可以和它细致的对角色进行设计，选 1

也可以直接开始创作第一章内容，选 2 （不建议）

如果你也懒的去细抠角色细节，就选 3

当然第 4 条就是留给你自由发挥的输出的！

其实这步就是为了让 AI 帮你生成角色档案的文档，这个文档在后面写作过程中如果发生了变化 ，你只需要一句：帮我更新角色档案人物关系，就直接在这个文档中更新了！

这样后续写长文的时候，它就可以保持与你的同频，方向一致！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_u722BawAAYpFt.jpg>)

角色档案里的内容非常多，也细致，生成后，会在文档里留存！

如果内容太多，看不明白，可以让 AI帮你生成表格，或者是以使用Mermaid语法可视化展示角色间的关系，我后期会升级本 skill 让展示更直观！

但是如果是.md 的文档，看起来就不方便，你可以利用 AI，给你产出更容易查看的其它格式文档。

## 接下来，开始第一章的正式写作！

在写第一章前，我在规则里写的是，需要先确定细纲，再开始写作正文，这样做的好处是，你要知道本章主要讲什么，有哪些故事细节，先把细节和走向确认好，这样内容的质量才有保障。

当然你可以跳过这个出细纲的步骤，直接让它写正文。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_u-ZTpbQAAVqza.jpg>)

细纲内容，只要你确认无误了，就可以开始创作了！

AI 写完了，并且给出了细纲要求与实际执行的一一对应，是不是很爽？是不是很严谨？是不是很有商业价值？

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_u_ccSbAAYRCAY.jpg>)

接下来，你可做的有：

1，继续第二章的细纲设计，或者直接下一章。

2，回看第一章产出内容，不断的与 AI 进行细节调整。

3，如果这时你已经写到了 100 多章了，你可以选择回顾已生成的所有文档，其实也就是让 AI 更新一下记忆。

这时我希望你了解一下这个 Skill 的功能指令都有哪些，为的是以后你可以直接在任何过程中，调用这个指令完成指定工作。

好，你可以在输入框中输入：help 或者 指令

它会给出所有规则指令列表：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_vA9OPa0AAW8Cm.jpg>)

在任意一章产出时，你都可以随时打断，让他去完成比如：AI 味检测，水文自检，氛围营造等多项个性化功能!

所以，这个 Skill并不是单纯的产出式技能指令，而是一个统合智能体！

你在写网文的过程中遇到的所有问题，都有涉及，这就需要你自己去探索了！

剩下的就简单了，就是不断的下一步，写新篇章了，而且写完的内容都已经在你的项目目录里躺着了！

下面是 AI 味自检的结果：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_vB8upWsAA_tEC.jpg>)

其它的操作，我就不演示了，在最后，我来对这个Skill写长文不幻觉，不忘记前面的一些规则说明进行介绍。

看到这些详细的规则设计，你就会明白这个 Skill 写网文的价值！

1，强制读取核心文档！

2，写本章内容时，要先看细刚，如果没有，就跳过。

3，一致性检查，这是保证前后逻辑和结构没有走偏。

4，创作时，分为短期、中期、长期记忆不同阶段的不同记忆设置！

5，有规则变化时，马上同步！

6，防幻觉机制！

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_vEEHlWkAAbX6U.jpg>)

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_vDhrmbAAIR14U.jpg>)

其中这里还有个文档：progress-tracking.md 它是长篇创作的记忆中枢：

1. 记录过去: 章节摘要、伏笔、角色变化

2. 指导现在: 下章重点、待办事项、当前状态

3. 规划未来: 近期章节规划、伏笔回收计划

更新频率: 每章创作后必须更新 使用频率: 每章创作前必须读取

其中这里还有个文档：progress-tracking.md 可以看到还没有创建，这个规则文档的作用是：

其它功能还有很多，不展开讲了，核心写作和流程已经讲解完毕！

大家自己去探索吧，这种乐趣需要你本人来体验！

所有产生的文档都会进到你的项目文件夹中，随时可查看！以后妈妈再也不担心我写长篇小说会卡文啦！

当然，我们的小说课也要同步去看哦，学会了写，你才能会指挥 AI 来创作！相辅相成！

今天的教程，就到这里，文中的 Skill 文档，“钱来有道”社群同学请单独和我联系获取，就不放在这里公布了！因为有商业价值，我不希望滥用，也杜绝那些薅羊毛党！

如果有缘，我们社群交流中再见！打完，收工！撒花🌸～

**正文**

This article was written along with my Madrona colleagues Anna Baird and Hope Cochran.
For years, founders had a clear target to aim for. Triple-triple-double-double was ambitious, sure, but it gave

---

**作者** Kushal Byatnal（@kushalbyatnal）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/kushalbyatnal/status/2016602943869293047  

**正文**

2.5 years ago, I picked the tech stack for [@ExtendHQ](<https://x.com/@ExtendHQ>) with one goal: ship fast as possible. That decision let us grow to $1M+ ARR with an engineering team of 3. Now as our volume has scaled 1000x, here's how those decisions have held up.

We made a bet on having a "boring" stack: React, Node, TypeScript (frontend and backend), Postgres, and Redis. That's it. We deliberately avoided specialized languages, complex microservices, and dependencies that can't be deployed on-prem.

2.5 years later, here's how that's going for us:

## What worked

The core stack is unchanged.

React, Node, TypeScript, Postgres, Redis — still the foundation, still works great. The shipping velocity is truly unmatched. If it ain't broke, don't fix it.

Monorepo was our best decision.

Being able to ship across the entire codebase in one PR is a superpower. And having all the context in one place makes Cursor and Claude dramatically more useful. One regret: I wish we'd put our docs repo in there too.

Designing for self-hosting from day 1.

When we set up our stack, we made sure everything could be deployed on-prem (no hard dependencies on niche vendors, no managed services we couldn't replicate). At the time, it felt like overkill.

But today, it unblocks deals. Self-hosted deployments are coming back in fashion because enterprises want to use LLMs on their most sensitive data. If we had to retrofit that today, it would be a 6-month nightmare of ripping out dependencies and re-architecting.

## What changed

We migrated to AWS.

We started off on one of the popular startup cloud providers, but had to migrate to AWS last year. Better stability was one part of it, but it also sped up sales cycles. When you're selling to F500s and public companies, their security teams want to see standard AWS architecture. It makes SOC2, compliance, and subprocessor + security reviews 10x easier.

We introduced Go and Rust (selectively).

We love TypeScript, but it’s not the tool for CPU-bound tasks. We spun up specific services in Go and Rust to handle compute heavy tasks like file conversion and Excel parsing.

## What didn't work

Postgres queues didn't survive.

At the MVP stage, using Postgres for job queues was fine. But at our current volume, it started locking up and we had some painful days of firefighting. We eventually brought in some amazing infra engineers and migrated our queue state to Redis. I wish I'd just started on Redis from day 1.

We migrated Auth providers.

We started with an open source auth tool and have been kicking ourselves ever since. It didn't support all the enterprise features we needed (SAML SSO, SCIM, etc). We eventually moved over to WorkOS (shout out @grinich)   and it's been smooth sailing since.

Overall: no major regrets. The boring stack let us move fast when it mattered most, and it's been flexible enough to evolve as we've scaled. 

I'd argue 99% of startups should adopt this same approach. We're all in extremely fast-moving spaces, and the simpler your stack, the faster you can keep up.

Boring tech wins.

---

**作者** 歸藏(guizang.ai)（@op7418）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/op7418/status/2016710786916536782  

**正文**

介绍一下我昨天开源这个视频包装 Skills 的工作原理：

简单来说这个 Skills 先用字幕智能分析生成特效配置，再由浏览器渲染逐帧生成特效图层。

最后通过视频合成把这些特效包装图层叠加到原始视频上的。

------

输入「视频 + 字幕」，先用 `content_analyzer.py` 从 SRT 里识别人物、章节、金句、术语、数据等，生成各种 Suggestion；

用户确认后写成统一的 `config.json` 配置，再交给渲染和合成管线。

`video_processor.py` 是主入口，负责解析命令行和配置、选择渲染后端（Browser 或 PIL）、按时间段分发不同组件的渲染任务。

主要渲染器 Browser 后端用 Playwright 打开 HTML 模板 + CSS 主题 + Anime.js 动画，通过 `initAnimation(config)` 初始化、`seek(timeMs)` 驱动逐帧截图输出 PNG

`templates/*.html` 定义 9 类组件，通过约定的 JS API 接收配置和时间；

`static/css/theme-*.css` 定义 notion/cyberpunk/apple/aurora 等主题，用 CSS 变量 + `data-theme` 切换风格。

新增组件只需：加一个 HTML 模板、在 `BrowserRenderer` 里加渲染方法，在 `video_processor.py` 注册处理逻辑、在 `content_analyzer.py` 增加对应 Suggestion 和配置校验；

新增主题则是新增一份 theme CSS 并在模板中引用。

**作者** BITWU.ETH 🔆（@Bitwux）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/Bitwux/status/2016362303994900821  

**正文**

昨天晚上 X 博主 may.crypto 用 Clawbot 在 Polymarket 交易，设置了一个简单的策略，一夜之间 AI 帮他从100美金赚到了347美金；

这是一个小的尝试，但是是一个大的趋势的缩影：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_uDH5YaoAA45nK.jpg>)

https://x.com/Bitwux/status/2016341735782416552

AI工长的下一步，就是一人公司。

未来是一人公司的高爆发期，也是所有普通人能够拥有的最大的机遇。

从 Dan Koe 的 《How I'd build a one-person business 》： [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VyR8nqD3sQ8](<https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VyR8nqD3sQ8>) 到肉眼可见的 Claude Code 的智能进化以及到这几天Clawdbot 成为真正的 AI Agent 帮你处理各类事件，

一人公司的雏形已然成形。

你可以让 Clawdbot 帮你订外卖，购物的时候讨价还价，甚至给他100美金让他去帮你挣钱，并且同时还自动重复性的完成每天必须完成的事情，他的存在就是你的一人公司的一个队伍。

那么从某种意义来讲，如果一个人能带好他的AI队伍，能为项目独立承担责任与风险，同时训练出了强大的全局视野和项目架构能力，往前一步，就是所有人都能自行创业，直面市场。

硅谷很多风险投资人和分析师都在期待三人甚至一人的独角兽公司能批量崛起，甚至chatGPT创始人 Sam Altman 直言：未来可能出现十亿级别的一人公司！

一人公司，俨然成为这个时代最佳的机会！

## 1️⃣什么是一人公司？

它不是“一个人做所有事”，而是“一个人拥有系统”

其实按照当下我的认知，我更喜欢把“一人公司”定义成：

公司里“唯一的全职员工/核心决策者”是你，但执行层面可以用 AI 工具、自动化流程、外包/合作伙伴 来扩展产能，他们都是你的 杠杆（leverage）：让你在同样的时间产生更高价值。

这里说下，很多人的误解，一人公司不是自由职业，他跟自由职业的关键区别：自由职业是以“工时”为核心资产（卖时间），项目越多越忙，天花板明显；

一人公司则是以“产品/标准化交付/流程”为核心资产（卖结果、卖系统），可以逐步把交付从“手工”变成“半自动/自动”，撬动杠杆拿到堪比超大公司的结果。

## 2️⃣我们来探讨下一人公司的可行性：

前面我说到过：从某种意义来讲，如果一个人能带好他的AI队伍，能为项目独立承担责任与风险，同时训练出了强大的全局视野和项目架构能力，往前一步，就是所有人都能自行创业，直面市场。

所以一人公司在 AI 的助理下变得更可行，但我同时也认为，不是“所有行业都适合”；

1）最适合一人公司的业务类型（优先级从高到低）

A. 数字化交付 + 高毛利

微型 SaaS / 插件 / 自动化工具；

模板、课程、训练营、知识库、会员制社群；

数据/报告/研究类订阅（如行业情报）；

B. 可产品化的服务（Productized Service）

“固定范围 + 固定价格 + 固定交付物”的服务例如：一周交付一套品牌视觉、一套投放素材、一个 SOP 系统、一个 Notion/飞书知识库搭建、一个 CRM 自动化等；

C. 咨询/顾问类（但要能标准化）

顾问天然容易变成“时间换钱”，但如果你能把方法论沉淀为模板/工具/流程包，就能逐步产品化‘

2）不太适合一开始就做“一人公司”的类型

重资产（生产制造、仓储物流强依赖）；

强监管/高合规成本（医疗、金融等很多细分领域）；

强线下交付、强人力服务密度（需要大量排班与现场）；

超长销售周期且需要复杂招投标的大 B 生意（可以起步小，但想靠一个人长期扛住会很痛苦）；

这里不是说不能做，而是：一人公司适合“轻资产 + 可复制 + 可远程交付”。其他类型更适合把“一人公司”作为早期阶段，而不是长期形态。

一人公司最容易失败的根源，不是 AI 不够强，而是：客单价太低 + 交付太重 + 获客太散最后变成“比上班更累，还不稳定”。那一人公司，这个AI杠杆，就失去了意义。

## 3️⃣为什么它会成为趋势：

Carta 的《Solo Founders Report 2025》显示：2019 到 2025 年上半年，新成立公司里“单人创始人”的占比从 23.7% 上升到 36.3%。

这说明“一个人创业/一个人公司”已经不是小众现象，而是在成为一种结构性变化。

以前一个产品从 0 到 1，最大的成本是：技术开发、设计、文案、客服、运营工具链、招人、磨合、管理成本；

现在很多环节能被 AI/自动化显著压缩：代码、原型、设计稿、落地页、广告素材、邮件序列、客服知识库、数据分析等都能加速，像 Replit 这类平台被媒体报道为推动“vibe coding（用自然语言做软件）”和一波 solo startup 浪潮。

再加上全球范围内，包括中国，因为经济下行，就业与组织形态发生变化：裁员与不确定性，更多人把“抗风险”放在第一位，让很多人更重视：收入自主权、技能可迁移性、多元收入来源。所以大家会更愿意在心理层面，寻求一人公司的机会，而不是只寻求稳定。

## 4️⃣如何做好一人公司：

这里出现了另外个误区，很多人看了前面的内容，会以为，如何做好一家一人公司的关键，就是“会用 AI”，

但我认为更重要的，是把公司做成可复制的系统：一人公司=定位 × 产品化 × 获客系统 × 自动化交付 × 风险管理；

核心是：你能不能把一件事，做成“不用你也能反复跑”的系统。

我来举个例子吧，比如在 Web3 里：

1）「我帮项目做增长」是一件事；

2）「我帮新项目，把空投规则、教程、流程一次性整理好，直接给用户用」是一件事；

前者听起来很厉害，但只有后者真的能收钱。

第二个关键，如果做一人公司，不要接“定制活”，只卖“固定的东西”。价格固定、内容固定、交付时间固定。

你今天交付这个，明天交付的还是这个。否则客户一多，你人先没了。

第三个关键：别只想着做出来，要想怎么卖出去。

AI 让“做东西”变得很便宜，但流量、信任、关系，依然很贵，一人公司能活下来的，不是技术最强的，是有人持续帮你转介绍的。

AI的本质很简单：它不是主角，是你的助理：帮你整理资料、帮你写模板、帮你做重复的事；

你只需要做三件事：选方向、做取舍、拿结果。

最后说一句很现实的：一人公司不是为了做大，而是为了先跑通。

先跑通一条能赚钱的路径，再决定要不要放大。

## 5️⃣最后的话

如果你可以有一套了然于心的商业逻辑，然后你可以训练出来的一整套 AI、工具、流程和系统。

当你能清楚地给 AI 下指令、设边界、控风险、拿结果，你其实已经在做一件事：以个人身份，直接面对市场。

这在过去，几乎是不可能的。而现在，它第一次对普通人开放。

一人公司，不是每个人都会成功，他还是需要巨大的能量和认知的，但它可能是这个时代，普通人第一次真正站上创业起跑线的机会。

这是生产关系在变。

能不能抓住，取决于你，能不能带好你的那支 AI 队伍。

---

**作者** Grant Lee（@thisisgrantlee）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/thisisgrantlee/status/2016557616953250143  

**正文**

# Stop focusing on PMF

Founders are obsessed with Product-Market Fit, understandably so. They track signups, watch churn numbers and check the reviews. And yeah, all that matters. Solving a problem is the way to enter a market and Product-Market Fit tells you people want what you're selling.

But it’s such a lagging indicator.

The question you should start with instead: “Am I developing a solution or a habit?”

“Habits Are Recurring Solutions to Recurring Problems” - James Clear

Not all problems are worth solving because not all problems recur. If you build something brilliant that solves a problem your user has once a year: filing taxes, booking a vacation rental, you don't have a habit. You have a utility. And most utilities are brutal businesses to start because you have to re-acquire that customer every single time they need you. Not impossible, but much harder.

To build a habit, you need to own a recurring moment in someone's day or week. A moment that keeps coming back. Think about the apps you use every single day without thinking. They're all sitting at the intersection of a recurring problem and a low-friction solution. That intersection is where habit-forming solutions live.

## The Hook Model

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_rq7l-bwAAb8nz.png>)

In Nir Eyal's Hooked, the loop is simple: Trigger, Action, Variable Reward, Investment.

But most products skip step one. They don't accurately identify the recurring problem. They fall in love with their solution before they understand the frequency of the pain.

Look at Slack. Why did it replace email for internal communications? Because the problem, "I need to coordinate with my team right now,” happens 50+ times a day. Email was technically a solution, but it was slow and asynchronous. It was designed for a different era.

By 2022, 57% of workers said they preferred messaging apps like Slack over email for internal comms. That's a habit shift. Slack fit the frequency of the problem. Email didn't.

At Gamma, we realized that knowledge workers face the problem "I need to communicate a complex idea professionally" at least weekly, sometimes daily.

The main existing solution was PowerPoint, a 40-year-old tool built for a world where people printed slides on transparencies. PowerPoint was massively high-friction. You spend 90% of your time aligning boxes and picking fonts, and 10% on the actual story.

Gamma became a habit because we made the solution as fast as the problem. You have an idea now. You need a deck now. Done.

## "What Would This Look Like If It Were Fun?"

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_rrAbVWMAMV4gk.png>)

This is another James Clear question that changed how we build. If your solution works but feels like work, you're fighting human nature. And human nature wins every time.

At Gamma, we asked ourselves: Why does making slides feel so painful? Because the tools are slow. They're tedious. They're designed for designers, not for people who just need to get an idea out of their head. We made it feel like playing with blocks instead of filling out tax forms.

Hooked products create internal triggers. Eventually, the push notifications don't matter anymore.

> If the user feels a specific discomfort or need, like boredom, confusion, or deadline pressure, and the solution they rush to automatically, is your product, that's when you know you've won.

## The First 30 Seconds Are Life or Death

The Investment Phase is the final step in the Hook Model. It's where users put something into your product, like content, data, customization, reputation. And this is why the first 30 seconds of your onboarding experience are everything.

Average 30-second retention for most apps is about 53-60%. That means nearly half your users are gone before they even see your value.

If a user invests time during that first session, like creating something, customizing a setting, inviting a teammate, they've just built switching costs without even realizing it. They've made your solution theirs.

> If you get users to invest in the first 30 seconds, they're exponentially more likely to stay. If you don't, they churn. And they almost never come back.

## Friction Reduction

Friction reduction is a sure-fire way to get the user to invest, and eventually create a habit.

What I learned from the first iPhone which came in 2007, is that every extra click, every extra decision, every moment of confusion is a crack in your habit loop.

I remember it took me 3 to 4 clicks to check my email on the iPhone, and when I did the same using my desktop PC, it took 12 to 15 clicks. I knew instantly how powerful reducing the ‘steps to outcome’ is.

The best products feel like they read your mind. They anticipate what you need before you realize you need it. It’s looks magical because it shows the understanding of the recurring problem better than anyone else.

The old way is building for a market. The new way is to build for a habit. Because markets shift. Habits stick.

**作者** meng shao（@shao__meng）

**正文**

第一个给普通人开箱即用的 Claude Code 出现了@happycapyai

Happycapy 把 Skills 想象成全新的「软件」，不用看代码或 CLI。Skills 在里面是每人都可以量身定制、即插即用的智能模块。配上沙盒和 CC 就是完整的 agent-native computer。
对很多用户来说，从意义上不再需要从零开始学怎么用。只需要告诉对应的 skill 或是新的 skill，「平时是怎么用 ppt 干活」、「平常怎么用文件」等等，它就会帮你把整个流程变成一个可复用、可叠加、可进化的技能。

使用方法三步搞定：
1. 先安装 Skills：直接从你的日常工作输出里抓取（比如你经常整理发票、写周报、做数据分析……），找对应的 skill 或是用 skill-creator 生成新的 skill
2. 让 AI 帮你打磨：把你自己的标准、习惯、偏好、公司模板、语气要求一股脑儿丢给 AI，说「照这个风格改」「要符合我们品牌调性」「必须包含这几项数据」让它自动迭代、优化 skill，直到完全符合你的口味。
3. 想跑流程的时候，直接拖拽一个或多个 skills，写一下任务就执行，不需要再写很长的 propmt，输出也是实时可见

以前你要花半天时间重复劳动，或是在不同平台转来转去。现在几秒钟搞定；以前非技术人员根本玩不转 Claude Code、Veo 这些模型，现在全在同一个地方，一句话就能调用。

**作者** Kyle Bigley 🥂（@kylebigley）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/kylebigley/status/2016202113508950296  

**正文**

Stop calling yourself a CEO when you are at $2M to $5M.

There are two phases to this game…

Founder mode and actual CEO mode.

Early on, you are not really a CEO, even if the title says so.

You're in the weeds, wearing every hat, doing things that don't scale.

And that is exactly what the job requires.

You need to be grinding because no one's going to care as much as you do.

If your team doesn't see you working hard, they won't be inspired to do the same.

That phase lasts different lengths for different companies, but it's necessary.

At some point though, you have to shift.

For me, it happened around $4M ARR when I realized I was still acting like a project manager.

I was micromanaging everything, finding pleasure in being involved in every detail.

Then I read Dan Martell’s book about buying back your time, and it finally clicked.

I calculated my replacement rate.

Anything under $500 an hour needed to be outsourced.

Design
Support
Copywriting
Development
Ads management
Customer success

All of it.

This year, we’re gonna hire an executive assistant, new live agents, partnerships manager, and community manager.

All the stuff I was handling in bits and pieces won't scale without dedicated specialists.

Now my job is setting culture, procedures, SOPs.

Managing people and reviewing their work instead of doing the actual work.

Working ON the business instead of IN the business.

Keeping close eyes on financials, roadmap, deadlines, big ticket items.

The transition feels weird because you go from being busy all the time to being less involved.

But that's the point... you're creating leverage and scale.

If the general is firing shots on the battlefield, something's seriously wrong.

The war can rarely be won without the general.

But it can definitely be lost if the general is too busy fighting individual battles to see the whole field.

**作者** Alex Xu（@alexxubyte）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/alexxubyte/status/2016192675012284609  

**正文**

Cursor recently shipped Composer, its agentic coding model, and shared that the agent can be ~4× faster! We worked with the Cursor team, particularly @leerob, to understand how the system is put together, and what drives the speed.

A coding agent is a system that can take a task, explore a repo, edit multiple files, and iterate until the build and tests pass.

Inside Cursor, a router first picks a suitable coding model (including Composer) to handle the request.

The system then starts a loop: retrieve the most relevant code (context retrieval), use tools to open and edit files, and run commands in a sandbox. Once the tests pass, the task is complete.

Cursor uses three key techniques to keep this loop fast:

1. Mixture-of-Expert (MoE): A sparse MoE architecture activates only a subset of model weights per token.

2. Speculative decoding: a smaller model drafts multiple tokens at once, then a larger model verifies them in parallel to reduce latency.

3. Context compaction: summarize older steps and keep only the active working set so the prompt stays relevant and short as iterations continue.

Full newsletter here: https://blog.bytebytego.com/p/how-cursor-shipped-its-coding-agent

**作者** Machina（@EXM7777）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/EXM7777/status/2016160442603995321  

**正文**

a year from now, two versions of you exist...

one is mass-applying to jobs with a generic resume, watching AI eat their industry, wondering when they'll "find time" to learn this stuff

the other is billing $200/hour for AI implementation, building tools that didn't exist six months ago, turning down clients because demand exceeds capacity

same starting point, different trajectory, and the split happens in the next 30 days

this is the curriculum that creates version two

i call it the Operator Toolkit: a specific sequence that builds AI skills in the order that maximizes compounding, where each phase unlocks capabilities for the next, and by day 31 you're not just using AI, you're deploying it as infrastructure

not another prompt engineering thread you'll bookmark and forget, not a course teaching 2024 techniques, not theory that sounds smart but produces nothing

> this is the path from overwhelmed to operational hands-on, current, specific 2-3 hours daily for 30 days

here's the thing most AI education gets wrong: they teach you tools before they teach you thinking, so you memorize prompts instead of developing intuition

we're going to fix that

let's build version two together

# the mental model you need to adopt

most AI education starts wrong

they teach prompt tricks before you understand why prompts work, so you're copying templates instead of adapting to situations

here's the foundation that makes everything else click... and once you have it, you'll never look at AI the same way again

## how AI actually reads your words

when you type "the bank was steep" the model has a decision to make: are you talking about money or a riverbank?

the attention mechanism solves this by weighing which surrounding words matter most, it's constantly asking "what context helps me understand this word?" and that simple insight explains 80% of why some prompts work and others fail

give the model clear context and it makes better decisions, starve it of context and it guesses

you've probably felt this without knowing why, some prompts produce exactly what you want while similar prompts produce garbage, the difference is usually context clarity

tokenization is how AI chunks your text before processing, roughly one token equals 3.5 characters or 0.75 words, and this matters because you're paying per token and hitting limits measured in tokens

context window is the AI's working memory, the total amount of text it can hold in mind at once

Claude Sonnet holds 200K tokens which is around 500 pages, GPT-5 holds 400K, and Gemini 3 Pro leads with 1M tokens (i made it simple here)

that 1M context window means you can feed Gemini an entire codebase or a book-length document and it keeps all of it in working memory, which changes what's possible for research and analysis completely... tasks that required breaking documents into pieces and losing coherence now work in a single pass

that being said, context windows have limits and you'll experience that when you spend more time with LLMs

## the parameter that matters most

temperature controls randomness on a 0-to-1 scale

at 0 the model gives you its most confident answer every time, at 1 it takes creative risks

set it low for factual queries and analysis, push it higher when you want unexpected ideas

this single parameter separates frustrating AI sessions from productive ones, most people never touch it and wonder why their results feel random

try this: run the exact same prompt twice at temperature 0, you'll get nearly identical outputs, then run it at temperature 1 and watch how different each generation becomes

## why AI lies to you and how to catch it

here's something counterintuitive: AI doesn't know what's true

it predicts what text is likely to come next based on patterns, and confident-sounding text patterns exist for both facts and fiction, so the model produces both with equal confidence

studies show nearly half of AI-generated citations are partially or completely fabricated... the model invents author names, journal titles, even URLs that don't exist

the fix isn't hoping they'll patch this, hallucination is structural, not a bug

instead: verify specific claims, use low temperature for factual queries, ask the model to acknowledge uncertainty, and build RAG systems that ground responses in real documents

the RAG approach is so effective it gets its own section later, but here's the preview: you can make AI reference your actual documents instead of its training data, which eliminates hallucination for domain-specific questions

## the January 2026 model landscape

how to pick AI models:

the "best" model changes based on what you're doing, and using the wrong one for your task is like using a screwdriver as a hammer... technically possible, frustrating, suboptimal

after testing everything available, this is how the landscape breaks down right now

## Claude from Anthropic owns three categories

coding - Claude Opus 4.5 leads the benchmarks and more importantly the community feedback, it truly is the best option right now

marketing and long-form writing - something about Claude's training makes it understand brand voice and nuance better than alternatives, run the same copywriting prompt across every major model and Claude consistently produces work that sounds human while others produce obvious AI slop (Kimi K2/2.5 is worth a try)

spreadsheet and business analysis - the new Claude in Excel integration processes multi-tab workbooks, explains calculations with cell references, and fixes formula errors, this alone is worth the subscription for anyone who spends more than an hour per week in spreadsheets

## Gemini 3 Pro from Google dominates research

that 1M token context window isn't just a bigger number, it's a different capability

you can upload an entire research corpus, a full codebase, months of meeting transcripts, and Gemini holds all of it while answering questions with full context... no more breaking documents into pieces, no more losing coherence between chunks

plus native Google Search integration means it pulls current information rather than hallucinating about things that changed after training cutoff

for any task requiring recent data or massive document analysis, Gemini wins and it's not close

## GPT-5 is a useful negative example

i'm not being contrarian for engagement, GPT-5 consistently produces the most generic, obviously-AI-written output

run the same prompt through Claude, Gemini, and GPT-5 and you'll spot the GPT output immediately, it has a particular blandness that's hard to describe but impossible to miss once you see it

understanding what mediocre AI output looks like helps you avoid producing it, so GPT-5 serves as a reference point for that

## Grok for real-time social analysis

if you need to analyze what's happening on X right now with fewer content restrictions, Grok is the tool

limited use case but nothing else does it as well

## the decision framework

stop asking "which AI is best" and start asking "what am I trying to do"

coding and technical writing -> Claude
 research requiring current information -> Gemini 
long document analysis -> Gemini (context window advantage) 
marketing copy and brand voice -> Claude 
spreadsheet work -> Claude with Excel integration 
social media analysis -> Grok 
image generation → Nano Banana Pro 
video generation → VEO 3.1 or Kling 2.6

this framework eliminates the decision paralysis that keeps most people switching between models and mastering none

but knowing which model to use is only half the equation... you also need to know how to communicate with them effectively, which brings us to the skill that compounds everything else

## prompt engineering in 2026

forget the clever tricks

the game changed, clarity beats cleverness now, and the people getting results are writing prompts that read like good briefs, not like magic spells

## format by model

Claude was trained with XML tags so it responds exceptionally well to structure like this:

GPT and Gemini work well with JSON when you need structured data back

plain text works for simple requests, markdown is a great overall option

the format isn't magic, it's about giving the model clear signals about what you want, XML tags function like section headers in a document, they reduce ambiguity and the model rewards clarity with better outputs

## chain-of-thought for hard problems

when you need the model to work through something complex, adding "let's think through this step by step" before asking for an answer significantly improves results

this isn't placebo, reasoning tasks show measurable improvement when you prompt the model to externalize its thinking process

use it for math, logic, multi-step analysis, and debugging

skip it for simple questions where the extra thinking adds nothing

## the system prompt formula

effective system prompts contain four elements:

role - who the AI should be, like "you are a senior financial analyst specializing in tech valuations"

behavior - how it should interact, like "ask clarifying questions before making assumptions and acknowledge when you're uncertain"

constraints - what it should avoid, like "do not give specific investment advice"

output structure - how to format responses, like "lead with a 2-sentence summary then provide supporting analysis"

a good system prompt converts a general-purpose AI into a specialized assistant for your specific workflow, and once you've built one that works, you can reuse it hundreds of times

now that you understand individual prompts, we need to zoom out... because the real leverage isn't in single prompts, it's in the information environment you create around your AI interactions

## context engineering: where the real leverage lives

prompt engineering was the 2024-2025 skill

context engineering is the 2025-2026 skill

the shift recognizes that individual prompts matter less than the information environment you create around your AI interactions

Shopify CEO Tobi Lutke defined it as "the art of providing all the context for the task to be plausibly solvable by the LLM"

this is where the Operator Toolkit diverges from surface-level AI education... most courses stop at prompts, but the people billing $200+/hour have moved to context architecture

## the four strategies

write - save context outside the active window using scratchpads and reference files the AI can access

select —-choose what enters context through RAG and dynamic retrieval rather than dumping everything in

compress - summarize verbose information before including it

isolate - use separate conversation threads or sub-agents for different contexts that shouldn't mix

## Claude Projects in practice

Claude Projects create persistent workspaces where uploaded documents stay accessible across every conversation

the setup: create a new project in claude.ai, upload relevant files, write custom instructions defining behavior, then every conversation in that project has full access to your knowledge base

you can also create knowledge containers in Claude Skills (i'd suggest you invest time working with Skills)

the insight most people miss: one focused project per task beats one massive project with everything

a project for "client proposals" with relevant case studies and pricing works better than a general "work stuff" project with hundreds of files competing for attention

## RAG for non-technical users

RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation and it sounds complex but the concept is simple: before answering your question, the system searches your documents for relevant information and includes that in the context

this grounds responses in your actual data rather than the model's training, which dramatically reduces hallucination and enables domain-specific expertise

NotebookLM from Google is free zero-code RAG: upload PDFs, docs, even YouTube videos, and suddenly you have an AI expert on your specific content that cites its sources

the RAG section later goes deeper on building custom systems, but these two tools cover 80% of use cases without touching code

## image generation: Nano Banana Pro for the win

late 2025 was supposed to be when AI image generation matured

instead one model leapfrogged everything else and reset expectations completely

## what Nano Banana Pro gets right

perfect text rendering: for years AI images couldn't spell, text came out garbled or mirrored or just wrong, now Nano Banana Pro generates correctly-spelled text in any style you specify, this single capability opens use cases that were impossible before like infographics, posters, social graphics with headlines

reasoning before rendering: the model thinks about your scene, considering composition and lighting and subject relationships before generating pixels, the result is images that feel intentional rather than random

search grounding: it can use Google Search to create factually accurate infographics about real topics, not just aesthetically pleasing nonsense

Simon Willison, who's one of the most respected voices in AI tooling, called it "the best available image generation model" and after testing everything i agree completely

## prompting Nano Banana Pro

forget the 2024 approach of loading prompts with "4k, trending on artstation, masterpiece" garbage

this model understands natural language, you describe what you want like you're briefing a photographer

the structure that works: subject with descriptive details, then action, then environment, then composition notes, then lighting, then any specific text requirements

for example: "a minimalist movie poster for a thriller, the title 'SILENT ECHO' in distressed sans-serif at the top, a lone cabin in a snowy forest viewed from above, high contrast black and white, title perfectly legible and centered"

specific is important here, describe the result you want rather than hoping the AI shares your taste

JSON prompting for Nano Banana is excellent too

## the other tools and when they matter

Midjourney V7 still produces the most artistic and cinematic output, particularly for stylized work where photorealism isn't the goal

ChatGPT image gen is fun for someone that's just playing with AI

Flux is the open-source option for those who want to run image generation locally

image generation is where most people stop exploring creative AI tools, but video generation has reached the point where specific use cases are production-ready

## video generation: impressive

i need to be honest here

AI video demos look incredible, the actual experience of using these tools is humbling

that said, they're production-ready for specific use cases and knowing which ones saves enormous frustration

## VEO 3.1 from Google

the most complete package available: native audio generation with synchronized dialogue and sound effects, up to 60 seconds through scene extension, 4K output, and vertical format support for social platforms

this is what you use when you need a finished clip with audio rather than just silent footage

## Kling 2.6 for cinematic realism

many "real" videos circulating on social media are Kling generations, the motion quality and physical consistency is remarkable

when you need the most realistic possible output for short clips, this is the tool

## what you need to know before using any video AI

5-10 seconds is the reliable range, longer generations degrade in quality and coherence

complex physics still fail sometimes, if your scene requires detailed movements expect multiple attempts

budget 3-10 attempts per usable clip, same prompt yields wildly different results

prompt like a director describing what the camera sees, not like a storyteller describing narrative: "medium shot of an old sailor gesturing toward the sea" works better than "a sailor tells stories about his adventures"

current sweet spot: social media shorts under 15 seconds, B-roll footage, product reveals, concept visualization

creative tools are powerful but the real transformation happens when AI can take action in the world on your behalf which brings us to coding...

## coding with AI even without coding skills

English is now a programming language

Andrej Karpathy called it "vibe coding" and the name stuck because it captures something real: you describe what you want, AI generates code, you run it and observe, then iterate based on results

non-developers are building functional tools this way, and developers are shipping 10x faster than before

## for developers: Claude Code and Cursor

Claude Code runs in your terminal and can read entire codebases, make multi-file edits, run tests, and create commits autonomously

by end of 2025 it hit $1B in annualized revenue, that growth rate reflects developers voting with their wallets after trying everything else

Cursor is an AI-first IDE built on VS Code, import your existing settings and you're productive immediately

these two tools together cover terminal work and IDE work, everything else is a downgrade at this point including GitHub Copilot which can't compete on any metric that matters

## for non-developers: build real things

Lovable takes natural language descriptions and produces complete web applications, no coding knowledge required

Bolt.new does similar rapid prototyping from plain English

Replit provides a browser-based development environment with AI assistance for those learning

the practical tasks this enables for people who never wrote code: automation scripts for file organization, data extraction from PDFs and websites, simple web tools for personal use, custom productivity apps

## automations that run while you sleep

this is where AI stops being a chat tool and becomes infrastructure

the difference between using AI and deploying AI is automation: systems that run without your involvement, processing inputs and producing outputs

## n8n is probably the easiest option

i tested every automation platform extensively and landed on n8n for clear reasons

it's open-source and self-hostable with unlimited free executions, which matters when you're running hundreds of workflow executions per day

Claude Code can generate n8n configurations from natural language descriptions: tell it what workflow you want, it produces the technical implementation

## the Claude Code to n8n pipeline

describe the workflow you want in plain English -> Claude Code generates the n8n configuration -> deploy it

this bypasses the learning curve for visual automation builders entirely, you're describing outcomes and receiving infrastructure

## MCP connects everything

Model Context Protocol is an open standard that lets AI systems connect to external tools and data sources

think of it as a universal adapter: implement MCP once and your AI can talk to Google Drive, Slack, GitHub, databases, whatever you need

Claude Desktop ships with pre-built MCP servers for common services, n8n can create custom MCP servers from workflows

## workflows that produce real value

content repurposing: publish a blog post and automatically generate LinkedIn, Twitter, and Instagram versions scheduled through Buffer: one piece of content becomes four without additional effort

customer feedback routing: new submissions get sentiment analysis, negative feedback routes to urgent Slack channels, support tickets created when needed: problems surface before they escalate

these aren't theoretical, they're running in production for businesses right now, and once you understand the pattern you can build custom versions for any repeating process

but the automation landscape is shifting as open source models approach closed-model capabilities

## open source models: study this now, run it soon

don't run local models yet for production work

the infrastructure isn't quite ready for daily use

but pay close attention because this is shifting fast, and the people who understand it early will have significant advantages when the switch happens

## what happened in 2025

open source caught up to closed models in ways that seemed impossible two years ago

Kimi K2 from Moonshot AI has over a trillion parameters and beats GPT-5 on major benchmarks while costing roughly 1/10th as much through API access

they just released 2.5 and it's a beast

DeepSeek V3.2 matches GPT-5 performance with 90% lower training costs and can be self-hosted

GLM 4.7 from Zhipu AI offers great coding capabilities

MiniMax M2.1 runs at a fraction of Claude's price while handling 1M token context windows comparable to Gemini

## the timeline we're looking at

right now: access open source models through APIs, OpenRouter provides a unified interface to most of them and lets you compare outputs directly

6-12 months: consumer hardware like upcoming Macs and gaming GPUs with high VRAM will run capable local models for daily use without cloud dependencies

12-24 months: open source likely matches or exceeds closed models for most practical tasks, at which point running AI locally becomes the norm rather than the exception

the Operator Toolkit prepares you for both worlds: closed models now, open source when the infrastructure catches up

understanding open source also prepares you for the next evolution: personal AI agents that run locally and take action autonomously

## building your custom knowledge assistant

RAG systems ground AI responses in your actual documents rather than training data, which solves the hallucination problem for domain-specific questions

this is where the Operator Toolkit pays off most directly: you build an AI expert on YOUR knowledge base that cites sources and doesn't make things up

## NotebookLM for zero-code RAG

Google's NotebookLM is kinda free, requires no setup, and works remarkably well (you should get a gemini subscription to enjoy the full experience)

upload PDFs, Google Docs, YouTube videos, or websites and the system becomes an expert on that content with inline citations

Audio Overviews generate podcast-style discussions of your documents, Mind Maps visualize complex topics, Deep Research in the Plus tier provides comprehensive analysis across your sources

this is the fastest path to a working knowledge assistant... under an hour from nothing to a functional system

## Claude Projects as an alternative

upload documents to a Claude Project and every conversation in that project references them automatically

more flexible than NotebookLM when you need to create outputs like documents and code rather than just query information

## going deeper with vector databases

for those building custom systems:

documents get split into chunks and converted to numerical representations called embeddings

those embeddings get stored in a vector database

when you ask a question, your query becomes an embedding and the database finds the most similar document chunks

those chunks plus your question go to the LLM which produces a grounded answer

this foundation prepares you for what's coming next: personal AI agents that don't just answer questions but take action

## personal AI assistants: a glimpse at the future

here's where things get genuinely weird...

we're watching the birth of AI assistants that aren't chatbots in browser tabs

i'm talking about AI that runs on your hardware, connects to every platform you use, remembers everything, and takes action autonomously

this is the end state the Operator Stack prepares you for... not just using AI tools, but deploying AI agents that work on your behalf

## Clawdbot is what Siri should have been

some guy released an open-source project called Clawdbot that's been spreading through tech circles rapidly enough to make Mac minis sell out in multiple markets

what makes it different from every assistant you've used:

> runs entirely on your hardware, not someone else's cloud connects to WhatsApp, Telegram, Slack, Discord, Signal, iMessage, and more persistent memory across every conversation can read/write files, control browsers, execute scripts, and build its own extensions

one user built a flight-querying CLI tool just by asking Clawdbot to create it

another built a personal reading app from their phone while putting their baby to sleep

people are using it to manage email, build tools, run research workflows... the use cases keep expanding as users discover what's possible

## the self-modifying future

Clawdbot can write code to extend its own capabilities

ask it to add a feature it doesn't have, it writes the code, tests it, and hot-loads the changes

someone captured the implication well: "it will be the thing that nukes a ton of startups, not ChatGPT like people meme about, the fact that it's hackable and more importantly self-hackable and hostable on-prem will make sure tech like this dominates conventional SaaS"

## trying it

Clawdbot is free on GitHub, you'll need an Anthropic or OpenAI API subscription or the ability to run local models

the recommended setup is a Mac mini running continuously but it works on any Mac or Windows or Linux machine (or a $5/mo VPS)

the setup is still technical, not for everyone yet

but if you want to see where personal AI is heading before Apple or Google figures it out, this is worth your time

2026 is the year of personal agents, the infrastructure exists, the early adopters are already living in this future

## the Operator Stack: why this sequence works

this curriculum follows a deliberate progression and the order matters

fundamentals first because without the mental model you're memorizing tricks instead of developing intuition, and intuition is what lets you adapt when tools change

prompt and context engineering next because these skills multiply the value of every AI interaction that follows, they're leverage points

creative and technical tools after that because image generation, video creation, and coding assistance have immediate professional applications where you can deliver value and get paid

advanced integration last because automation, open source awareness, and custom knowledge systems transform AI from a tool you use into infrastructure that works for you while you sleep

## the single highest-leverage move

>build a Claude Project for a task you do repeatedly

>upload relevant documents, write custom instructions that define behavior, and suddenly you have a specialized assistant that saves hours every week

>not hypothetical hours, real hours, the kind you can redirect toward work that matters or reclaim for your life outside work

## resources worth bookmarking

Anthropic Prompt Guide - official documentation with patterns that work

OpenAI Tokenizer - visualize how text becomes tokens, essential for understanding context limits

Andrej Karpathy's LLM videos - foundational understanding that ages well as tools change

NotebookLM - free RAG without code, working knowledge assistant in under an hour

OpenRouter - unified access to every major model including open source options

## the path forward

30 days from now, two versions of you exist

one completed the Operator Toolkit and can do things that seemed impossible a month ago: building tools, automating workflows, deploying AI infrastructure that runs without constant attention

the other is still collecting bookmarks, still planning to start, still waiting for the "right time"

same starting point, different trajectory

the window matters because the gap between AI-fluent and AI-confused is widening every month, the people who build these skills now will have compound advantages that grow over time, while the people who wait will face an increasingly steep climb

the roadmap is here

the tools work

30 days, 2-3 hours daily, and you're operating instead of observing

what happens next is your choice, but the choice is time-sensitive, and waiting has a cost

let's build version two

**作者** 超级个体｜柿子（@yaohui12138）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/yaohui12138/status/2016146124277743906  

**正文**

为什么有PM背景的人,用Vibe Coding接外包能轻松年入20w

而纯技术背景的开发者反而容易翻车

我花了3个月深度跑通AI自动化外包这条路,发现了一个反直觉的真相：

真正值钱的不是你会用Claude Code或Cursor

而是你能不能听懂客户那句"我想要一个自动化系统"背后藏着的10个没说出口的需求

先说市场有多大
2026年1月,全球前三大自由职业平台：(Upwork/Fiverr/Freelancer)的AI工作流自动化订单同比暴涨144%

客单价从去年的$800-$1500,直接跳到$3000-$5000

为什么

因为企业发现雇一个全职开发团队做内部自动化,成本是$15万/年起步

但找一个懂AI工具的自由职业者,3周交付一个能跑的系统,只要$5000

这笔账太好算了

PM思维凭什么是降维打击：

我之前在百度做PM时有个习惯

拿到需求第一件事不是想"怎么实现"

而是问3个问题:

用户真正想解决的问题是什么？
他为什么现在才想解决这个问题？
如果做出来他最担心什么会出错？

这套方法迁移到AI自动化外包上,直接变成了我的核心竞争力

为什么Vibe Coding适合PM,不适合纯开发者

看看2026年最火的AI编程工具对比就知道了

Claude Code：
最适合"描述需求→AI生成→人工调整"的迭代循环,现在占据Anthropic 12%的营收(大概)

Cursor:代码补全强,但需要你本身就懂技术架构

Windsurf:界面友好,但处理复杂业务逻辑时容易"理解偏差" 4 5

PM的优势在于你本来就习惯：

"用自然语言描述清楚一个功能应该长什么样"

这恰好是Vibe Coding的核心能力——把模糊的业务逻辑,转化成AI能理解的精确指令

我现在的工作流是:

和客户视频通话30分钟,梳理业务流程(这是PM的基本功)
画一个简单的流程图

标注每个节点的输入输出(用Figma,5分钟搞定)

然后用AI直接口喷n8n流程

跑MVP测试,找到边界case,再让AI针对性修复

交付前录一个10分钟的Loom演示视频,教客户怎么用

全程我没写超过50行代码

但客户愿意付$3000-$5000,因为我解决的是他们的业务问题,不是技术问题

接单路径:从0到第一个$5000

很多人卡在"不知道去哪儿找客户"

我的经验是:别去竞争最激烈的地方

国内平台(猪八戒/程序员客栈):价格被压得很低,客户预期也乱

国外平台才是真正的机会

Upwork现在84%的自由职业者在用AI工具,但真正会"AI自动化咨询"的人还很少

我的策略是:

在Upwork上把Profile定位成"AI Workflow Automation Specialist"(不是Developer)

案例展示用Loom视频,不是GitHub链接(客户看不懂代码,但能看懂一个系统怎么运行)

报价比纯技术外包高30%,但强调包含需求梳理+培训+1个月技术支持

第一单最难

我当时是主动找了3个本地小企业(咖啡店/健身房/会计事务所)

免费帮他们做一个简单的"Instagram评论自动回复"工作流

做完让他们写推荐信,再把这些案例放到Upwork上

最容易踩的3个坑

不要过度依赖AI，要做需求确认
客户说我要一个CRM系统,你直接让AI生成

结果交付时发现他们其实只需要一个Google Sheets + 自动化表单

解决方法:先做一个3-5页的需求确认文档,列出所有功能点和数据流,让客户签字确认再开工

工具选错了,返工成本巨高

n8n适合复杂逻辑,但部署麻烦

make界面友好,但高级功能要付费

Zapier最贵,但客户接受度最高

解决方法:根据客户技术水平选工具。

如果客户是非技术背景,优先用Zapier或Make,别为了省钱选n8n,后期维护会被投诉

没有设置边界,陷入无限改需求

解决方法:合同里明确写"包含3次迭代修改,超出部分按$150/小时计费"。

这不是为了多收钱,是为了让客户认真思考自己到底要什么

最后说一句大实话

Vibe Coding不是让你变成程序员

而是让你用PM的方式,把AI当成你的外包技术团队

你的核心价值永远是:听懂需求、拆解问题、设计方案、控制交付

代码交给Claude写就行了

如果你还在纠结"我不会编程能不能做"

那你可能还没理解这件事的本质

2026年最值钱的能力,不是写代码

而是知道该让AI写什么代码

**正文**

我强烈建议所有在做vibe coding小游戏的人都去玩一下这个网站 http://neal.fun ，

我今天终于把全部的 @nealagarwal （一个创意天才）产品都玩了一遍，基本上玩的过程就是“这是他做的？卧槽这也是？”

夯：
> https://neal.fun/internet-roadtrip/ 一个大家集体投票决策一个小车要开到Google Maps哪里的游戏

> https://neal.fun/infinite-craft/ 靠不同单词碰撞出新单词的游戏，这个游戏在llm刚有起势的时候爆火了一次

> https://neal.fun/absurd-trolley-problems/ 你有一个扳手可以改变火车的走向的各种变体，你能看见大家投票的分布，里面有好多值得思考的小哲思

顶级：
> https://neal.fun/logos-from-memory/ 根据你的记忆画品牌的logo

> https://neal.fun/not-a-robot/ 一些无敌难的证明你不是机器人的验证

> https://neal.fun/password-game/ 让你设置一个密码，而要包含数字、字母、罗马字母甚至代表当前的月食状态的表情包等等等很多的要求

人上人：
> 特别！让我！惊喜！的是： https://neal.fun/auction-game/ ，这个是根据名画来猜当时的拍卖价格，跟我做的guess the fdv的想法真的好像，我是想通过这个来表达对过高定价的不屑来着。（能和这种我欣赏的人有很像的想法让我超级开心哈哈哈哈）

> https://neal.fun/dark-patterns/ 一些互联网的黑色小技巧，比如如何骗你加好友/购物等

我的感觉就是他会把生活里的一些观察无限放大，比如嫌人机验证太麻烦，我就给你弄的无敌麻烦；嫌弃对设置密码要求限制太多，我就给你弄的无敌安全的密码；嫌弃公司在网站设置的分享链接太多，我就给你弄的一整页的分享链接。

然后更多的其实就是一些可视化的展示，比如公司赚钱的速度/花掉比尔盖茨的钱、人生进展等等...

**作者** Ming Yin（@kalasoo）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/kalasoo/status/2016346057228386466  

**正文**

今天用 Kimi K2.5 干活，用真实的感受看看是不是比 Opus 4.5 好，以及 1/8 成本
---
昨天 Opus 4.5 烧了我 $80（我不觉得花的多有什么价值，最重要的是做出有趣的东西）
今天用 Kimi K2.5 干活，用真实的感受看看是不是比 Opus 4.5 好，以及 1/8 成本
---
昨天 Opus 4.5 烧了我 $80（我不觉得花的多有什么价值，最重要的是做出有趣的东西）
我来总结一下我今天使用的整体体验

1. 成本：今天用 K2.5 总工作量大概是昨天用 Opus 4.5 的 1/3，昨天烧了 $80，今天用 Kimi 大概花了 $6，所以从成本上大概是 6*3/80=22.5%节省

2. 质量：不像是之前从 Opus4.5 切换到 K2, GLM-4.7 会明显觉得差了一点（很多细节都差了一点，但只要用的够充足一下子就能感觉出来）。但是这次 K2.5 我没有这个感觉，我能体会到它回复和做事情的流程和 Opus4.5 不太一样，像是换了个人但不觉得变差了。

3. 蒸馏：虽然我没有做严谨的论证，也不是专业训模型的，但很明显有蒸馏 Claude 的痕迹，能问出来 ...（求官方不要打我，而且蒸馏的“正义性”也是个待论证的问题）

---

总结：如果之前你的主力是 Sonnet 4.5 或者用 Opus 4.5 做复杂度中等的事情，感觉 K2.5 现在便宜的程度可以切换。但依据 @glow1n 的用 SOTA 理论，我会继续使用 Opus 4.5/4.5 Thinking/Thinking MAX 在我认为重要的事情上，及时更贵一些。

**作者** ℏεsam（@Hesamation）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/Hesamation/status/2016316188029030507  

**正文**

he’s so right. AI isn’t a tool skill, it’s a management skill. the people who integrate well with AI aren’t just good at prompting or coding, they’re good at specific “senior-level” skills. according to a Microsoft study, these 6 skills matter most:
1. context assembly. knowing what information to provide from which sources and why. ai is sensitive about the context quality.
2. quality judgement. you must know when to trust ai output and how to verify it. which parts are likely reliable or hallucinated. 
3. task decomposition. avoid throwing entire projects, break into manageable chunks.
4. iterative refinement. whether you trust that first output or abandon the whole task, or treat it as a starting point.
5. workflow integration. whether you treat it as a side tool or an integrated capability.
6. frontier recognition and knowing when you’re operating outside the ai capabilities.

just as you wouldn’t take a whole app idea and give it to an intern and expect anything to work, you need to chunk up the problem into small pieces, delegate them to the right number of agents with the right skills, orchestrate them, and quantify their output.

the mindset shift from simply prompting good to managing AI has happened slowly. the ones who are good at AI are gradually learning to become good managers or seniors without explicitly realizing.

Gamma + Claude MCP = on-demand slide decks

I gave Claude a presentation topic. It pulled relevant data from my G Drive + supporting graphics from the web

I answered a few Qs on format, and Gamma generated a (beautiful!) deck in my pre-saved style 👇 
You can also edit or regenerate in the same interface - just tell Claude what you want to change, and Gamma will execute it!

With access to email, GDrive, etc. there are tons of use cases here - ex. "update the deck with the latest data" or "make a new version for client X"
You can set this up by going to Claude Connectors, browsing Connectors, and configuring Gamma. 

You'll log in with your Gamma account, and it can then pull from your past presentations, templated styles, etc.

**作者** Santiago（@svpino）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/svpino/status/2016242526706102629  

**正文**

LobeChat is an open-source, multi-model interface with 70,000 GitHub stars, 14,000 forks, and 6 million users.

It's really, really good!

Now, they turned it into @lobehub to solve one of the problems that I've had with every other agent platform.

Every platform treats agents as disposable: You spin one up, it does a task, you throw it away.

This is fine for simple stuff, but it doesn't scale to anything more complex.

LobeHub is introducing something new: agents as teammates.

You build agent groups that work together.

• A supervisor agent orchestrates every workflow
• Individual agents handle specialized tasks
• These agents work in parallel
• Agents can challenge and cross-check each other

The team ran one sample on both LobeHub and Manus:

• LobeHub took 2:58 minutes, $0.46 average cost
• Manus took 9:01 minutes, $2.98 average cost

That's 3x faster and 6.5x cheaper!

The difference here is that Manus uses VM-based web browsing, while LobeHub connects directly to source files.

A few things that stand out:

• LobeHub supports any model: Claude, Gemini, or whatever you want.

• LobeHub uses human-in-the-loop by default. You confirm before agents execute.

• You can discover and use agent groups that others have built.

When testing LobeHub Desktop and Claude Cowork, they appear to have very similar performance. LobeHub has the advantage of routing tasks to multiple models, giving it an edge.

For example, Claude Cowork couldn't extract the subtitles of a video, but LobeHub did because it routed the task to Gemini.

The attached video shows LobeHub tailoring a resume for different job positions. A bunch of agents work in parallel to generate different versions of the resume.

从这个对话我对 OpenAI 后面的模型还有点期待，既然他们意识到 ChatGPT 模型写作能力的问题，去调整应该不是太难的事。
另外 GPT-5.2 的代码能力是真的很强，比 Opus 4.5 厉害。
还有很重要一点，Codex CLI 不能定位为单一的 Coding Agent，或者必须推出与 Claude Code 相当的通用 Agent，哪怕是 CLI
从这个对话我对 OpenAI 后面的模型还有点期待，既然他们意识到 ChatGPT 模型写作能力的问题，去调整应该不是太难的事。
另外 GPT-5.2 的代码能力是真的很强，比 Opus 4.5 厉害。
还有很重要一点，Codex CLI 不能定位为单一的 Coding Agent，或者必须推出与 Claude Code 相当的通用 Agent，哪怕是 CLI
也不完全是cli，模型也要优化，比如现在 codex 模型：
1. 速度太太慢，虽然稳，但是日常任务美人受的了这速度
2. 编程之外任务执行结果并不太好
3. 写作能力太差，无法去做好需要“写作”相关的任务，很多任务都需要写作能力，比如发邮件、写推文、写文章
https://x.com/tapopat/status/2016215014533955672?s=20
Codex 产品设计上还有个问题就是喜欢替你做主：“为你好”

但每个人需求都不一样，不同的人有很多定制需求，现在模型的能力还没有智能到刚好帮你做你期望结果的地步。

**作者** 苍何（@canghe）

**正文**

今天看到腾讯的 CodeBuddy Code 2.0 重磅更新，已经全面支持 Skills 了。

我当时就来劲了，在高铁上直接就用 CodeBuddy Code 手戳了个小红书封面图生成 Skills。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_ptXXVbAAMofKP.jpg>)

全程耗时 15 分钟就完成了这个 Skills 的开发，他能根据你的主题自动的帮你生成小红书封面图。

你无需关注任何细节，你只需要在对话框中输入以下提示词：

>生成小红书封面图，主题为：「输入你的主题」

CodeBuddy Code 就能自动调用 xiaohongshu-skills 生成一张精美的小红书封面图。

比如今天是腊八，我输入主题为：腊八节南北方习俗。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_ptj2UbAAYijVh.jpg>)

这张封面图就做好了，直接就可以拿去发小红书，毕竟真的还不错。

这个就是在底层调用的 nb2 。但是做成 Skills 我觉得还蛮合适的，因为他是重复的可被抽离的技能。

我也把这个 Skills 直接开源到 GitHub 上面去了，大家有想要玩的，直接下载就好了。

>文末会附上怎么使用，感兴趣的可以点赞并滑到底，看下怎么玩。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_ptpAka4AAkbxX.jpg>)

最近 Skills 在 AI 圈内火出来天际，但是圈外可能还不是很清楚。我之前也写过相关教程。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_ptwMPbAAIMPqi.jpg>)

在这里再简单哔哔几句，基于我这段时间的理解。

我觉得 \*\*Skills 更像是 Agent 的 SOP，他封装了提示词、MCP 工具、脚本等，是大模型的技能包。\*\*

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pt5OgbAAIoaU4.jpg>)

就拿我做的这个小红书 Skills 来说，他内部封装了生成小红书封面图都提示词，以及迁移图片重命名的脚本等。

拿到这个 Skills，就能让大模型稳定输出小红书封面图片，并移动到指定文件夹。

现在很多人以为还只有 Claude Code 可以使用 Skills，其实像开源的 OpenCode 配合上插件也能用。

现在也已经 88.5 k 的标星了，而且有 1.2 k 的 PR，更新迭代非常迅速。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_puBS6agAAkQMW.jpg>)

可见大家对 Claude Code 早就已经有想法了。

但国内其实还是多少有些上手难度，好在腾讯的 CodeBuddy Code 也率先支持 Skills 了，对国内用户也很友好。

这次 CodeBuddy Code 2.0 的迭代还是有点东西的，我截了一张官方公众号图，大家可以感受一下。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_puGzTbAAEhUo1.jpg>)

讲真，CodeBuddy Code 一开始推出，我就有用，并有写过一篇文章：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_puRMAaYAA2_GB.jpg>)

在生态集成和便利性这块没的说，这次 2.0 不仅开放了 SDK 支持被集成，还支持 Plugin 插件市场。

国内外顶尖模型，像 GPT-5.2-Codex、Gemini 3 Pro、DeepSeek-V3、GLM-4.7 都完全支持。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_puXzfbsAAvvap.jpg>)

不过不知道 default 是啥模型，我感觉还挺好用的，小红书这个 skill 就是用的 default 模型，速度很快，指令理解也很强。

下面分享下我是如何通过 CodeBuddy Code 来做小红书 skills 的，也会分享该如何使用以及该如何\*\*无感迁移 Claude Code 神级配置\*\*。

>文章人肉打磨了不少时间，喜欢可以点赞转发给需要的朋友呀。

#  安装 CodeBuddy Code

在终端中输入命令：

\`\`\`

npm install -g @tencent-ai/codebuddy-code@latest

\`\`\`

安装完成后，选择项目文件夹，然后输入：codeBuddy。

选择登录方式即可。如果选择国内版，\*\*支持微信登录\*\*，如果选择海外版支持 Github 或者 Google 邮箱登录。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pul73XcAAqta_.jpg>)

没问题的话你就能顺利进来了。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pusp-bAAEUp4z.jpg>)

我发现现在最新版本的 codebuddy code 能直接生图了，这在全球也算是首个能支持生图的 CLI 了。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_puyWuakAAQ5u1.jpg>)

国内版用的是混元的文生图模型，新增 \`ImageGen\` 工具，可以直接根据文本描述生成图片。支持自定义尺寸、风格、质量等多种参数。

通过 \`/model:text-to-image\` 命令查看和切换可用的文生图模型

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pu5z4bAAA0Nou.jpg>)

国际版盲猜也会很快上线 nb2 模型，那这就有意思了。

也就是我这个小红书的 skills 完全就可以通过提示词来控制，也希望后面支持配置生图提示词。

## 开发 Skills

要想做一个Skills，最重要的是安装一个做 Skills 的 Skills。

在. codebuddy/skills 文件夹下面会有 skill-creator，你也可以用自然语言让 codebuddy code 帮下载。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pvGB5a4AA7fRj.jpg>)

然后输入需求：

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pvNItbAAAtCIA.jpg>)

没一会功夫，就已经完成了这个 skills 的创建。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pvS8RWQAABM7o.jpg>)

速度还是非常快的。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pvavdawAAQ0s3.jpg>)

使用 Skills

重新加载 codebuddy code，直接输入需求，它就能自动 match 小红书 skill，然后生成精美的小红书图片。

大家也可以下载 GitHub 上的 skills，放到自己的 skills 目录。

![Article Image](<https://pbs.twimg.com/media/G_pvzUabAAAQ2GD.jpg>)

GitHub 地址如下：https://github.com/freestylefly/xiaohongshu-skills

>也欢迎大家给 star。

你需要输入自己的 API Key，默认的是 nb2 模型，你可以看着改。

或者让 codebuddy code 帮你改，都非常方便了。

好啦，感谢你阅读到这里，我们下一期见。

**作者** Logan Gott（@LoganTGott）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/LoganTGott/status/2016347538559783265  

**正文**

1. Post 6-7x a week (not 2-3)
2. Send 200 connection requests weekly to qualified leads
3. DM every single new connection within 24 hours
4. Follow up 2-3 times on non-responders
5. Post 2x+ lead magnets a week

Then do that for 90 days.

Nobody tells you how to ACTUALLY implement this though... I will below

## 1. POST 6-7X A WEEK (NOT 2-3)

"but Logan I don't have time to post every day isn't that overkill??"⠀

Here's why 2-3 posts a week doesn't work:

Your ICP scrolls LinkedIn once, maybe twice a day. If you post Monday and Thursday, you're invisible Tuesday, Wednesday, Friday, Saturday, Sunday. That's 5 days where someone could be searching for exactly what you offer and you're nowhere to be found.

LinkedIn's algorithm also rewards consistency. When you post daily, the algorithm starts to understand your content patterns. It knows when to push your stuff. It knows who engages. It learns your audience.

Post twice a week and the algorithm treats you like a stranger (unfortunately that's the algo rn)

The content mix matters too:

- 2 posts/week: top of funnel (stories, personal life, shallow ideas that get engagement)

- 3 posts/week: middle of funnel (pain points, how-tos, carousels showing expertise)

- 2 posts/week: bottom of funnel (case studies, results screenshots, lead magnets)

→ Top of funnel gets people onto your profile.
→ Middle of funnel positions you as the expert.
→ Bottom of funnel converts them into leads.

Skip any layer and the funnel breaks.

Most founders only post middle of funnel content. Endless "how to" posts that get decent engagement but zero leads. Or they only post bottom of funnel and wonder why nobody cares about their case studies - they haven't earned the trust yet.

The other thing nobody talks about: batch your content.

I write all my content on Monday. Ideation happens Saturday. By Tuesday morning, my entire week is scheduled. I'm not scrambling at 6am trying to think of something for that day forcing me to write bad content.⠀

If you're "finding time" to post every day, you're doing it wrong. Block 2-3 hours once a week and knock it all out.

## 2. SEND 200 CONNECTION REQUESTS WEEKLY TO QUALIFIED LEADS

This is where people get weird, they tell me you can't send 200 connections a week or you'll get banned lol

LinkedIn CLEARLY STATES you can send 200 connection requests per week with Premium/ Sales Navigator. It's built into the platform. You're not doing anything against policy.

Here's how to actually do this:

Open Sales Navigator. Go to lead filters. Start qualifying:

Company headcount: 11-50 or 51-200 employees (this usually means $1M-$20M revenue since you can't filter by revenue directly)

Job title: founder, co-founder, CEO, president. Skip "owner" - that pulls in local businesses and older companies that aren't your ICP from my experience

Geography: start with US. The lead quality is typically higher and they have budget.

Industry: pick ONE industry per list. Don't mix software and consulting and ecommerce in the same list. Your messaging needs to be specific.⠀

An extra filter to use if your market is large after filtering is the "Posted on linkedin" filter. It helps guarantee you're targeting active users who will actually see your connection request and messages.

Save them to a lead list. Manually add them page by page until you hit ~1,000 leads. This takes 25-30 minutes (I watch YT golf while doing it lol). That's one month of outreach about.

Before you just start connecting with anyone, hover over the company name. Check estimated revenue. If they're under $1M, skip them. If the founder looks like they started last week with zero content and a few connections, skip them.⠀

You get 200 connections a week. Don't waste them on unqualified leads.

Why manual and not automation?

I've had clients get shadow banned from automation tools. LinkedIn can detect it. One day your posts just stop getting engagement and you have no idea why. It's not worth it for the 30 minutes you save.

YES I know automations CAN work, just depends if you're willing to lose your account potentially.⠀

Send 40 connection requests per day, Monday through Friday. 40 x 5 = 200. Simple math and M-F because that's when people are active.

## 3. DM EVERY SINGLE NEW CONNECTION WITHIN 24 HOURS

When someone accepts your connection, you have a window.

They're thinking about you. They just looked at your profile. They made a decision to let you into their network. That's the warmest they'll ever be.

Wait 3 days and that window closes. Now your DM feels random. "who is this person and why are they messaging me?"

Do this:

Go to LinkedIn → My Network → Connections → sort by "recently added"

Scroll through. Anyone who accepted from your lead list, open their profile. Do 30 seconds of research. Then DM them

This can be 1 of 2 ways

A soft pitch, super personal, getting to know them

Qualifying softly then pitching.

Second is a straightforward pitch

Quick but identifying their problem and showing off a solution with proof.

## 4. FOLLOW UP 2-3 TIMES ON NON-RESPONDERS

⠀

This is where almost everyone quit and it's insane to me.

You do all the work - build the lead list, send connections, write the first DM - and then when they don't respond, you just... give up?

You NEED to realize people are busy. They saw your message. They meant to respond. They got distracted. They forgot. Who knows.⠀

Following up isn't annoying. It's professional. What's annoying is "just bumping this to the top of your inbox :)" or "circling back on this" - that's lazy.

⠀

Here's a 3-message follow up sequence:⠀

Follow up 1 (3 days after initial DM): add value⠀

Send them something relevant. A case study. A free resource you wrote about their industry. A post relevant to them.

"Hey \[name\] thought you might find this interesting. We just helped a \[similar company\] do \[result\]. Here's the breakdown: \[link\]"

You're not asking for anything. You're giving.

Follow up 2 (3 days after follow up 1): short and direct⠀

"Hey did you get a chance to see my last message?"

This one qualifies them. If they're not interested, they'll either ignore or tell you. Either way, you have clarity.

Follow up 3 (3-5 days after follow up 2): close the loop

"Hey \[name\] I know you're busy, no worries. If you ever want to chat about \[result\], I'm around. Hope business is going well."

This one works because it's polite and gives them an easy out. Weirdly, this is often the one that gets responses. People feel bad that you're "giving up" and finally reply.⠀

Don't send follow ups on Saturdays or Sundays. If day 3 lands on a weekend, push to Monday.⠀

Most people don't follow up because they're scared of being annoying or of failing.

But think about it - if you send 800 connections a month, maybe 400 accept, you DM all 400, maybe 25 respond to the first message...

That's 375 people gone. 375 potential conversations you're leaving on the table because you didn't send two more messages.

## 5. POST 2X+ LEAD MAGNETS A WEEK

Lead magnets are an unfair advantage hardly anyone uses (and usually incorrectly if they do).

Here's what happens when you post a lead magnet:

- People have to comment to get the resource
- Comments boost your post in the algorithm
- More people see the post
- More people comment
- More people visit your profile
- More people see your other content
- You collect emails and can nurture them off-platform

It's a flywheel. One post does the work of five.

But most lead magnets suck. 

They're focused on DELIVERABLES instead of OUTCOMES.⠀

Bad: "comment 'guide' to get my 10-page linkedin content template"

Who cares about a template? What does the template DO for me?

Good: "this is the exact 15-page strategy my client used to add $112,000 in revenue. comment 'strategy' and I'll send it over"

Now I know what I'm getting. I know the outcome. I want that.

Structure of a high-converting lead magnet post:


Hook: create FOMO or call out a massive outcome
Body: stack proof on proof
Make it feel exclusive
Call to action⠀⠀

So many people post lead magnets and never actually send the resource. SEND THE RESOURCE.

Add "we must be connected for me to DM you" - otherwise you'll burn Sales Navigator credits on inmails or just not be able to send it at all.

The FUNNEL behind the lead magnet:

Don't just DM them the document. That's leaving money on the table.

1. DM them: "here's the resource you requested - \[link to opt-in page\]"

2. Opt-in page collects their email, then redirects to the actual resource

3. Resource has a CTA at the end to book a call

4. Email sequence (3 emails over 3 days) nurtures them and pushes toward booking

Now you have their email. You can nurture them. You can retarget them. You're not dependent on them seeing your LinkedIn content again.

## WHY 90 DAYS?

This is the filter.

Most founders do this for 2-3 weeks. They post consistently. They send connections. They DM people. And nothing happens.

So they quit.⠀

Weeks 1-4: the algorithm is learning who you are. Your audience is learning who you are. Your messaging is getting dialed in. You're figuring out what angles work.

Weeks 5-8: momentum starts building. Posts perform slightly better. Replies to DMs increase. You book a few calls. Nothing crazy but you can see it working.

Weeks 9-12: compounding kicks in. The audience you built in month 1 is now seeing consistent content for 60+ days. Trust is established. They've seen your case studies. They've read your lead magnets. When you DM them or they see your post, they're ready to talk.

Over 90 days that's 180+ posts. 2,400+ connections. Thousands of DMs. Dozens of lead magnets.

The system works. You just have to work the system long enough for it to compound.

If you want this implemented 100% done for you - content, outbound, funnels, all of it... link is in my bio. We'll see if you're a fit.

Otherwise, you have the playbook. Go execute.

**作者** meng shao（@shao__meng）  
**貼文連結** https://x.com/shao__meng/status/2016321643405312130  

**正文**

Manus 全面集成 Agent Skills

Manus 认为它们的原生架构（Sandbox 环境、Shell 执行能力）和 Agent Skills 是“绝配”：
· 一键固化经验：用户可以将一次成功的复杂交互过程，通过“Build a Skill with Manus”功能一键封装成个人技能，实现最佳实践的标准化和复用。
· 团队技能库：团队成员可以共享经过验证的高效技能，降低新手门槛，实现组织内部知识的资产化。
· 精准触发控制：支持通过斜杠命令（如 /SKILL_NAME）手动强制加载特定技能，确保 Agent 行为的确定性。

Manus AI 正在将 SimilarWeb、YahooFinance 等内置工具“技能化”，从黑盒 API 变为用户可感知、可调用的组件。
